        <i>
         Cuando
         <b>
          seas
         </b>
        </i>
        (also
        <b>
         fueres
        </b>
        <i>
         )
        </i>
        mayor, comprenderás.
        <i>
         (Spanish)
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        'When you
        <b>
         are
        </b>
        older, you'll understand.'
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Dar-se-á/Se dará o prêmio à primeira pessoa que
         <b>
          disser
         </b>
         a resposta correta.
        </i>
        (Portuguese)
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Se dará el premio a la primera persona que
         <b>
          diga
         </b>
         (also
         <b>
          dijere
         </b>
         ) la respuesta correcta.
        </i>
        (Spanish)
       </dd>
       <dd>
        'The prize will be given to the first person who
        <b>
         says
        </b>
        the right answer.'
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Irregular_verbs">
        Irregular verbs
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Comparison_of_Portuguese_and_Spanish&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Irregular verbs">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       A number of irregular verbs in Portuguese change the main vowel to indicate differences between first and third person singular:
       <i>
        fiz
       </i>
       'I did' vs
       <i>
        fez
       </i>
       'he did',
       <i>
        pude
       </i>
       'I could' vs
       <i>
        pôde
       </i>
       'he could',
       <i>
        fui
       </i>
       'I was' vs
       <i>
        foi
       </i>
       'he was',
       <i>
        tive
       </i>
       'I had' vs
       <i>
        teve
       </i>
       'he had', etc. These vowel differences stem from vowel raising (
       <a href="/wiki/Metaphony_(Romance_languages)" title="Metaphony (Romance languages)">
        metaphony
       </a>
       ) triggered historically by the final
       <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
        -
        <b>
         ī
        </b>
       </span>
       of the first-person singular in Latin. Spanish maintains such a difference only in
       <i>
        fui
       </i>
       'I was' vs
       <i>
        fue
       </i>
       'he was'. In all other cases, one of the two vowels has been regularized throughout the conjugation and a new third-person ending
       <i>
        -o
       </i>
       adopted:
       <i>
        hice
       </i>
       'I did' vs
       <i>
        hizo
       </i>
       'he did',
       <i>
        pude
       </i>
       'I could' vs
       <i>
        pudo
       </i>
       'he could', etc.
      </p>
      <p>
       Contrarily, Spanish maintains many more irregular forms in the future and conditional:
       <i>
        saldré
       </i>
       'I will leave',
       <i>
        pondré
       </i>
       'I will put',
       <i>
        vendré
       </i>
       'I will come',
       <i>
        diré
       </i>
       'I will say', etc. Portuguese has only three:
       <i>
        farei
       </i>
       'I will do',
       <i>
        direi
       </i>
       'I will say',
       <i>
        trarei
       </i>
       'I will carry'.
      </p>
      <p>
       Portuguese drops -
       <i>
        e
       </i>
       in "irregular" third-person singular present indicative forms after ⟨z⟩ and ⟨r⟩, according to phonological rules:
       <i>
        faz
       </i>
       'he does',
       <i>
        diz
       </i>
       'he says',
       <i>
        quer
       </i>
       'he wants', etc. Spanish has restored -
       <i>
        e
       </i>
       by analogy with other verbs:
       <i>
        hace
       </i>
       'he does',
       <i>
        dice
       </i>
       'he says',
       <i>
        quiere
       </i>
       'he wants', etc. (The same type of analogy accounts for
       <i>
        fiz
       </i>
       vs
       <i>
        hice
       </i>
       'I did' in the past tense. In nouns such as
       <i>
        paz
       </i>
       'peace',
       <i>
        luz
       </i>
       'light',
       <i>
        amor
       </i>
       'love', etc.
       <i>
        -e
       </i>
       was dropped in both languages and never restored).
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Prepositions">
        Prepositions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Comparison_of_Portuguese_and_Spanish&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Prepositions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Contractions">
        Contractions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Comparison_of_Portuguese_and_Spanish&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Contractions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       In Spanish the prepositions
       <i>
        a
       </i>
       ('to') and
       <i>
        de
       </i>
       ('of, from') form
       <a href="/wiki/Contraction_(grammar)" title="Contraction (grammar)">
        contractions
       </a>
       with a following masculine singular definite article (
       <i>
        el
       </i>
       'the'):
       <i>
        a
       </i>
       +
       <i>
        el
       </i>
       &gt;
       <i>
        al
       </i>
       , and
       <i>
        de
       </i>
       +
       <i>
        el
       </i>
       &gt;
       <i>
        del
       </i>
       . This kind of contraction is much more extensive in Portuguese, involving the prepositions
       <i>
        a
       </i>
       ('to'),
       <i>
        de
       </i>
       ('of, from'),
       <i>
        em
       </i>
       ('in'), and
       <i>
        por
       </i>
       ('for') with
       <a href="/wiki/Article_(grammar)" title="Article (grammar)">
        articles
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Demonstratives" title="Demonstratives">
        demonstratives
       </a>
       regardless of number or gender.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       All four of these prepositions join with the definite article, as shown in the following table:
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable">
       <tr>
        <th>
         Preposition +
         <br/>
         definite article
         <br/>
         (Portuguese)
        </th>
        <th>
         <i>
          a
         </i>
        </th>
        <th>
         <i>
          de
         </i>
        </th>
        <th>
         <i>
          em
         </i>
        </th>
        <th>
         <i>
          por
         </i>
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="text-align:center; background:#dbdbdb;">
         <i>
          o
         </i>
         <br/>
         (masc.sing.)
        </td>
        <td align="center">
         <i>
          ao
         </i>
        </td>
        <td align="center">
         <i>
          do
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          no
         </i>
         <sup>
          1
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          pelo
         </i>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="text-align:center; background:#dbdbdb;">
         <i>
          a
         </i>
         <br/>
         (fem.sing.)
        </td>
        <td align="center">
         <i>
          à
         </i>
         <sup>
          2
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td align="center">
         <i>
          da
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          na
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          pela
         </i>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="text-align:center; background:#dbdbdb;">
         <i>
          os
         </i>
         <br/>
         (masc.pl.)
        </td>
        <td align="center">
         <i>
          aos
         </i>
        </td>
        <td align="center">
         <i>
          dos
         </i>
         <sup>
          1
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          nos
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          pelos
         </i>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="text-align:center; background:#dbdbdb;">
         <i>
          as
         </i>
         <br/>
         (fem.pl.)
        </td>
        <td align="center">
         <i>
          às
         </i>
        </td>
        <td align="center">
         <i>
          das
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          nas
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          pelas
         </i>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       <small>
        <sup>
         1
        </sup>
        These Portuguese contractions include some potential "
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/False_friends" title="False friends">
         false friends
        </a>
        " for the reader of Spanish, such as
        <i>
         no
        </i>
        (Port. 'in the', Sp. 'no, not') and
        <i>
         dos
        </i>
        (Port. 'of the', Sp. 'two').
       </small>
       <br/>
       <small>
        <sup>
         2
        </sup>
        In European Portuguese,
        <i>
         a
        </i>
        is pronounced
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ɐ]
        </span>
        , while
        <i>
         à
        </i>
        is pronounced
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [a]
        </span>
        . Both are generally
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [a]
        </span>
        in most of Brazil, although in some accents such as
        <i>
         carioca
        </i>
        and
        <i>
         florianopolitano
        </i>
        there may be distinction.
       </small>
      </p>
      <p>
       Additionally, the prepositions
       <i>
        de
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        em
       </i>
       combine with the demonstrative adjectives and pronouns as shown below:
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable">
       <tr>
        <th>
         Preposition +
         <br/>
         demonstrative
         <br/>
         (Portuguese)
        </th>
        <th>
         <i>
          de
         </i>
        </th>
        <th>
         <i>
          em
         </i>
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="text-align:center; background:#dbdbdb;">
         <i>
          este
         </i>
         (masc.sing.)
         <br/>
         <i>
          esta
         </i>
         (fem.sing.)
         <br/>
         <i>
          estes
         </i>
         (masc.pl.)
         <br/>
         <i>
          estas
         </i>
         (fem.pl.)
        </td>
        <td align="center">
         <i>
          deste
         </i>
         <br/>
         <i>
          desta
         </i>
         <br/>
         <i>
          destes
         </i>
         <br/>
         <i>
          destas
         </i>
        </td>
        <td align="center">
         <i>
          neste
         </i>
         <br/>
         <i>
          nesta
         </i>
         <br/>
         <i>
          nestes
         </i>
         <br/>
         <i>
          nestas
         </i>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="text-align:center; background:#dbdbdb;">
         <i>
          esse
         </i>
         (masc.sing.)
         <br/>
         <i>
          essa
         </i>
         (fem.sing.)
         <br/>
         <i>
          esses
         </i>
         (masc.pl.)
         <br/>
         <i>
          essas
         </i>
         (fem.pl.)
        </td>
        <td align="center">
         <i>
          desse
         </i>
         <br/>
         <i>
          dessa
         </i>
         <br/>
         <i>
          desses
         </i>
         <br/>
         <i>
          dessas
         </i>
        </td>
        <td align="center">
         <i>
          nesse
         </i>
         <br/>
         <i>
          nessa
         </i>
         <br/>
         <i>
          nesses
         </i>
         <br/>
         <i>
          nessas
         </i>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="text-align:center; background:#dbdbdb;">
         <i>
          aquele
         </i>
         (masc.sing.)
         <br/>
         <i>
          aquela
         </i>
         (fem.sing.)
         <br/>
         <i>
          aqueles
         </i>
         (masc.pl.)
         <br/>
         <i>
          aquelas
         </i>
         (fem.pl.)
        </td>
        <td align="center">
         <i>
          daquele
         </i>
         <br/>
         <i>
          daquela
         </i>
         <br/>
         <i>
          daqueles
         </i>
         <br/>
         <i>
          daquelas
         </i>
        </td>
        <td align="center">
         <i>
          naquele
         </i>
         <br/>
         <i>
          naquela
         </i>
         <br/>
         <i>
          naqueles
         </i>
         <br/>
         <i>
          naquelas
         </i>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The neuter demonstrative pronouns (
       <i>
        isto
       </i>
       'this'
       <i>
        isso
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        aquilo
       </i>
       'that') likewise combine with
       <i>
        de
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        em
       </i>
       – thus,
       <i>
        disto
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        nisto
       </i>
       , etc. And the preposition
       <i>
        a
       </i>
       combines with the "distal" demonstratives (those that begin with
       <i>
        a-
       </i>
       ) to form
       <i>
        àquele
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        àquilo
       </i>
       , etc.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Portuguese contractions mentioned thus far are obligatory. Contractions can also be optionally formed from
       <i>
        em
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        de
       </i>
       with the indefinite article (
       <i>
        um
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        uma
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        uns
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        umas
       </i>
       ), resulting in
       <i>
        num
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        numa
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        dum
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        duma
       </i>
       , etc. and from the third person pronouns (
       <i>
        ele
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        ela
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        eles
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        elas
       </i>
       ), resulting in
       <i>
        nele
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        nela
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        dele
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        dela
       </i>
       , etc. Other optional contractions include
       <i>
        de
       </i>
       with
       <i>
        aqui
       </i>
       &gt;
       <i>
        daqui
       </i>
       ('from here').
      </p>
      <p>
       The Spanish
       <i>
        con
       </i>
       ('with',
       <i>
        com
       </i>
       in Portuguese) combines with the prepositional pronouns
       <i>
        mí
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        ti
       </i>
       , and
       <i>
        sí
       </i>
       to form
       <i>
        conmigo
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        contigo
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        consigo
       </i>
       ('with me', 'with you', 'with him-/herself '). In Portuguese this process not only applies to the pronouns
       <i>
        mim
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        ti
       </i>
       , and
       <i>
        si
       </i>
       (giving
       <i>
        comigo
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        contigo
       </i>
       , and
       <i>
        consigo
       </i>
       ), but also is extended to
       <i>
        nós
       </i>
       and, in those varieties which use it,
       <i>
        vós
       </i>
       , producing
       <i>
        connosco
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        conosco
       </i>
       in Brazilian Portuguese) and
       <i>
        convosco
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span id="Personal_.22a.22">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id='Personal_"a"'>
        Personal "
        <i>
         a
        </i>
        "
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Comparison_of_Portuguese_and_Spanish&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title='Edit section: Personal "a"'>
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Spanish employs a preposition, the so-called "personal
       <i>
        a
       </i>
       ", before the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Direct_object" title="Direct object">
        direct object
       </a>
       of a
       <a href="/wiki/Transitive_verb" title="Transitive verb">
        transitive verb
       </a>
       (except
       <i>
        tener
       </i>
       ) when it denotes a specific person(s), or domestic
       <a href="/wiki/Pet" title="Pet">
        pet
       </a>
       ; thus
       <i>
        Veo
        <b>
         a
        </b>
        Juan
       </i>
       'I see John';
       <i>
        Hemos invitado
        <b>
         a
        </b>
        los estudiantes
       </i>
       'We've invited the students.' In Portuguese, personal
       <i>
        a
       </i>
       is virtually non-existent, except before
       <i>
        Deus
       </i>
       'God':
       <i>
        louvar
        <b>
         a
        </b>
        Deus
       </i>
       'to praise God',
       <i>
        amar
        <b>
         a
        </b>
        Deus
       </i>
       'to love God'.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ir_a_versus_ir_para">
        <i>
         Ir a
        </i>
        versus
        <i>
         ir para
        </i>
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Comparison_of_Portuguese_and_Spanish&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Ir a versus ir para">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Quite common in both languages are the prepositions
       <i>
        a
       </i>
       (which often translates as "to") and
       <i>
        para
       </i>
       (which often translates as "for"). However, European Portuguese and Spanish distinguish between going somewhere for a short while versus a longer stay, especially if it is an intended destination, in the latter case using
       <i>
        para
       </i>
       instead of
       <i>
        a
       </i>
       . While there is no specified duration of stay before a European Portuguese speaker must switch prepositions,
       <i>
        a
       </i>
       implies one will return sooner, rather than later, relative to the context. This distinction is not made in English and Brazilian Portuguese
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       . In Spanish the distinction is not made if the duration is given in the context (maybe implicitly), and in this case
       <i>
        a
       </i>
       is generally preferred.
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Fui
         <b>
          a
         </b>
         l mercado cerca de mi casa.
        </i>
        (Spanish)
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Fui
         <b>
          a
         </b>
         o mercado perto de/da minha casa.
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         Fui
         <b>
          para
         </b>
         o mercado perto de/da minha casa.
        </i>
        (European and Brazilian Portuguese)
       </dd>
       <dd>
        'I went
        <b>
         to
        </b>
        the market near my house.' [temporary displacement]
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         El presidente anterior fue exiliado
         <b>
          a
         </b>
         Portugal.
        </i>
        (Spanish)
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         O presidente anterior foi exilado
         <b>
          para
         </b>
         Portugal.
        </i>
        (European and Brazilian Portuguese)
       </dd>
       <dd>
        'The former president was exiled
        <b>
         to
        </b>
        Portugal.' [permanent, or more lasting displacement]
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       Note, though, in the first example,
       <i>
        para
       </i>
       could be used in Portuguese if in contrast to a very brief period of time.
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Não fico muito tempo, só um minuto. Tenho que/de ir
         <b>
          para
         </b>
         o mercado.
        </i>
        (Portuguese)
       </dd>
       <dd>
        'I can't stay long, only a minute. I have to go
        <b>
         to
        </b>
        the market.' [pending task or appointment]
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       In informal, non-standard Brazilian Portuguese,
       <i>
        em
       </i>
       (in its original form or combined with a given article in a contraction, yielding
       <i>
        no
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        na
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        numa
       </i>
       , etc.), often replaces the preposition
       <i>
        a
       </i>
       from standard Portuguese.
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Vou
         <b>
          na
         </b>
         padaria.
        </i>
        (non-standard Brazilian Portuguese)
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Vou
         <b>
          à
         </b>
         padaria.
        </i>
        (standard Portuguese)
       </dd>
       <dd>
        'I'm going
        <b>
         to the
        </b>
        bakery.'
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Fui
         <b>
          numa
         </b>
         festa ontem.
        </i>
        (non-standard Brazilian Portuguese)
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Fui
         <b>
          a uma
         </b>
         festa ontem.
        </i>
        (standard Portuguese)
       </dd>
       <dd>
        'I went
        <b>
         to a
        </b>
        party yesterday.'
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       Such a construction is not used in Spanish or in European Portuguese.
      </p>
      <p>
       In Portuguese the preposition
       <b>
        até
       </b>
       can also be used when the duration of the stay is expected to be short or when there is a specific reason for going somewhere. In Spanish
       <b>
        hasta
       </b>
       has the same meaning and function.
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Vou
         <b>
          até
         </b>
         a praia.
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Voy
         <b>
          hasta
         </b>
         la playa.
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        'I'm going to the beach.'
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hacia_and_para">
        <i>
         Hacia
        </i>
        and
        <i>
         para
        </i>
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Comparison_of_Portuguese_and_Spanish&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Hacia and para">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Spanish has two prepositions of direction:
       <i>
        para
       </i>
       ('for', including 'headed for [a destination]') and
       <i>
        hacia
       </i>
       ('toward [not necessarily implying arrival]'). Of them, only
       <i>
        para
       </i>
       exists in Portuguese, covering both meanings.
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Este regalo es
         <b>
          para
         </b>
         ti
        </i>
        . (Spanish)
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Este presente é
         <b>
          para
         </b>
         ti
        </i>
        . (Portuguese)
       </dd>
       <dd>
        'This gift is
        <b>
         for
        </b>
        you.'
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Aquel/Ese avión va
         <b>
          hacia
         </b>
         Brasilia.
        </i>
        (Spanish)
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Aquele avião voa
         <b>
          para
         </b>
         Brasília.
        </i>
        (Portuguese)
       </dd>
       <dd>
        'That airplane is flying
        <b>
         toward
        </b>
        Brasília.'
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       Colloquially,
       <i>
        para
       </i>
       is often reduced in both languages: to
       <i>
        pa'
       </i>
       in Spanish,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and to
       <i>
        pra
       </i>
       (sometimes written
       <i>
        p'ra
       </i>
       and this form may be used in literature) or
       <i>
        pa
       </i>
       (only in slang in Portugal and Rio de Janeiro, and not permitted in writing) in Portuguese. Portuguese
       <i>
        pra
       </i>
       , in turn, may join with the definite article:
       <i>
        pra
       </i>
       +
       <i>
        o
       </i>
       &gt;
       <i>
        pro
       </i>
       (BP) or
       <i>
        prò
       </i>
       (EP),
       <i>
        pra
       </i>
       +
       <i>
        a
       </i>
       &gt;
       <i>
        pra
       </i>
       (BP) or
       <i>
        prà
       </i>
       (EP), etc.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In reference to the slang option
       <i>
        pa
       </i>
       , these become:
       <i>
        pa
       </i>
       +
       <i>
        o
       </i>
       &gt;
       <i>
        pò
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        pa
       </i>
       +
       <i>
        a
       </i>
       &gt;
       <i>
        pà
       </i>
       , etc.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span id=".22Going_to.22_future">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id='"Going_to"_future'>
        "Going to" future
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Comparison_of_Portuguese_and_Spanish&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title='Edit section: "Going to" future'>
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Both languages have a construction similar to the
       <a href="/wiki/Going-to_future" title="Going-to future">
        English "going-to" future
       </a>
       . Spanish includes the preposition
       <i>
        a
       </i>
       between the conjugated form of
       <i>
        ir
       </i>
       "to go" and the infinitive:
       <i>
        Vamos
        <b>
         a
        </b>
        cantar
       </i>
       "We're going to sing" or "Let's sing" (present tense of
       <i>
        ir
       </i>
       +
       <i>
        a
       </i>
       + infinitive). Usually, in Portuguese, there is no preposition between the helping verb and the main verb:
       <i>
        Vamos cantar
       </i>
       (present tense of
       <i>
        ir
       </i>
       + infinitive). This also applies when the verb is in other tenses:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Ayer yo iba
         <b>
          a
         </b>
         leer el libro, pero no tuve la oportunidad.
        </i>
        (Spanish)
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Ontem eu ia ler o livro, mas não tive oportunidade.
        </i>
        (Portuguese)
       </dd>
       <dd>
        Yesterday I was going
        <b>
         to
        </b>
        read the book, but never had the chance.
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_differences_in_preposition_usage">
        Other differences in preposition usage
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Comparison_of_Portuguese_and_Spanish&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Other differences in preposition usage">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       While as a rule the same prepositions are used in the same contexts in both languages, there are many exceptions.
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Nuestros gastos
         <b>
          de
         </b>
         energía.
        </i>
        (Spanish)
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         (Os) nossos gastos
         <b>
          com
         </b>
         /
         <b>
          de
         </b>
         energia.
        </i>
        (Portuguese)
       </dd>
       <dd>
        Our energy expenses.
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Voy
         <b>
          a
         </b>
         votar
         <b>
          por
         </b>
         Juan.
        </i>
        (Spanish)
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Vou votar
         <b>
          em
         </b>
         /
         <b>
          no
         </b>
         João.
        </i>
        (Portuguese)
       </dd>
       <dd>
        I'm going to vote
        <b>
         for
        </b>
        John.
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Orthography">
        Orthography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Comparison_of_Portuguese_and_Spanish&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Orthography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Alphabet">
        Alphabet
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Comparison_of_Portuguese_and_Spanish&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Alphabet">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The traditional
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_alphabet" title="Spanish alphabet">
        Spanish alphabet
       </a>
       had 28 letters, while the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_alphabet" title="Portuguese alphabet">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       had 23. Modern versions of recent years added
       <i>
        k
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        w
       </i>
       (found only in foreign words) to both languages. Portuguese also added
       <i>
        y
       </i>
       for loanwords.
      </p>
      <p>
       With the reform in 1994 by the 10th congress of the Association of Spanish Language Academies, Spanish alphabetization now follows the same pattern as that of other major West European languages. Prior to this date, however, the digraphs
       <i>
        ch
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        ll
       </i>
       were independently alphabetized. For example, the following
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Surnames" title="Surnames">
        surnames
       </a>
       would be put in this order:
       <i>
        Cervantes, Contreras, Cruz,
        <b>
         Ch
        </b>
        ávez, Dávila
       </i>
       . Many Spanish dictionaries and other reference material still exist using the pre-reform rule of alphabetization.
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <b>
         Current Spanish alphabet
        </b>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Spanish_orthography" title="Spanish orthography">
         Spanish alphabet reform of 1994
        </a>
        )
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <dl>
         <dd>
          <big>
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/A" title="A">
             a
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/B" title="B">
             b
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/C" title="C">
             c
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/D" title="D">
             d
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/E" title="E">
             e
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/F" title="F">
             f
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/G" title="G">
             g
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/H" title="H">
             h
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/I" title="I">
             i
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/J" title="J">
             j
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/K" title="K">
             k
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/L" title="L">
             l
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/M" title="M">
             m
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/N" title="N">
             n
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/%C3%91" title="Ñ">
             ñ
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/O" title="O">

            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/P" title="P">
             p
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/Q" title="Q">
             q
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/R" title="R">

            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/S" title="S">

            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/T" title="T">
             t
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/U" title="U">
             u
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/V" title="V">
             v
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/W" title="W">
             w
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/X" title="X">
             x
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/Y" title="Y">
             y
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/Z" title="Z">
             z
            </a>
           </i>
          </big>
         </dd>
        </dl>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        Digraphs
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <dl>
         <dd>
          <big>
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Ch_(digraph)" title="Ch (digraph)">
             ch
            </a>
            <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ll_(digraph)" title="Ll (digraph)">
             ll
            </a>
            <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rr_(digraph)" title="Rr (digraph)">
             rr
            </a>
            <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gu_(digraph)" title="Gu (digraph)">
             gu
            </a>
            <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qu_(digraph)" title="Qu (digraph)">
             qu
            </a>
           </i>
          </big>
         </dd>
        </dl>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <b>
         Current Portuguese alphabet
        </b>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Language_Orthographic_Agreement_of_1990" title="Portuguese Language Orthographic Agreement of 1990">
         Portuguese Language Orthographic Agreement of 1990
        </a>
        ) introducing
        <i>
         k
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         w
        </i>
        and
        <i>
         y
        </i>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <dl>
         <dd>
          <big>
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/A" title="A">

            <a href="/wiki/B" title="B">

            <a href="/wiki/E" title="E">
             e
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/F" title="F">

            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/G" title="G">

            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/H" title="H">
             h
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/I" title="I">
             i
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/J" title="J">
